< review>
I was looking for yoga in Cupertino and didn't try anything else after going to Bright Heart. It's a welcoming and (literally) warm place. I was afraid of the heated aspect of the classes, but it's not too much and I've learned to love it. The classes follow the same general flow, but the teachers add in their own touches. The one thing they have in common is they all kick your butt, incorporating strength and pilates exercises more so than most yoga classes. They have a lot of classes on the schedule so it's easy to find one that works for you if you buy a pass.< /review>

<pictures>None< /pictures><Resp>None</Resp><Gmap_id>0x8091064af8307f37:0x37fb85a885afa334<//Gmap_id></record></dataset><record>
< Review>
Coming from the PNW where coffee addicts are made, I was surprised to have had such great tasting coffee at this local cafe.  While packing for a vacation to visit family, finding coffee stands was on my checklist next to toothbrush and snacks.  It's a necessity for me.  As part-owner for a local business in Washington, supporting local shops are important.  Google suggested Cafe Rome and, like a tourist, I had my phone lead the way. The barista was great and for a decent price I had one of the most satisfying iced coffees.  I enjoyed the drink and the atmosphere.  The next morning I waited patiently for the shop to open, Folgers just wasn't cuttin' it.  I ordered what I typically get at my hometown coffee stand and again was pleased with my drink.  I wanted to order a bag of grounds to brew a pot when I got home and share with my other half.  There wasn't one available, but the barista was really sweet and had given a small bag of locally roasted coffee beans for me to have.  I am very happy with the service and will stop in on my next visit to California. #localcoffeshop #coffeeaddiciton #coffeconnoisseur #shoplocal<//Review>

< review>
There's only a few pizza places I will actually get pizza from in the Bay area. Zachary's hands down is one of them. This is the first time I've eaten at this location usually I go to the one on College Ave. I went to their website and pre-ordered the pizza online. They use the toast app which I'm sure they don't get the full amount but it was just easier for me to do it this way. I really don't like using third-party apps because they get into the business's profit and it hurts them a lot more during the pandemic. But at least do this app you can also leave a tip with the employees. part of the office away from each other. it's really hard for me to choose just one pizza but we went with a carne pizza. We've done parties at work where I'll order three or four different types of pizza for 20 people. And two slices will definitely fill up a person with an average stomach. If you're a big eater you probably get three slices in because the slices are so thick and full of goodness.<//review>

Chris James< /username>
<date>1368031048205</date>< rating>
2<//rating>
<text>I always take my MB Sprinter van to Mercedes dealers for maintenance because I have always received excellent service:  top notch parts, knowledgeable mechanics who stand behind their work, and extraordinary customer service.  This has proven to be accurate for 3 out of the last 4 MB dealers I have visited UNTIL I visited MB Santa Rosa.

I arrived on time for my appointment to investigate a steering vibration and Matt checked me in.  He was pleasant enough and we had a quick discussion of the symptoms my van was experiencing.  I retired to the lounge and prepared to wait for an hour or so.  About 4 hours later I finally heard from Matt that the mechanic didn't find any mechanical problems with the steering and that this vibration issue was caused by my overly worn tires.  I was surprised to hear this because (a) my tires were not yet worn down to the wear bar, (b) the vibration didn't feel like a tire issue to me, and (c) it took 4 hours to figure this out?.  But this was a Mercedes mechanic, the best in the business, so I trusted them.  Matt offered to sell me a set of 4 tires but the order wouldn't arrive for four days.  I declined because I was under a deadline to continue my drive south to Mexico and couldn't wait around that long.

My van was driven back around front and I was also disappointed to see that it had not been washed.  The three other dealers I have visited all washed my van without being asked, but apparently this isn't offered at Santa Rosa.  I paid the service charge (I guess being told your tires are slightly worn is considered service) and hit the road.  At least if my van had been washed I would have felt like I got a little something for my money.

I called a few shops along my route but none of them had the tires in stock.  Since Matt told me it was just a tire problem and not a mechanical problem, it didn't seem serious so I decided to drive to Mexico and get new tires on the return trip.

On the drive back north I noticed the vibration worsening so I took my van to Mercedes Benz of Van Nuys.  Within about two minutes of arriving, the Service Consultant and a mechanic pinpointed the cause of my problem.  It was not the tires, it was a loose steering linkage located under the hood.  They explained to me how dangerous it was because I could have lost steering at any moment when the bolt loosened all the way out.   They fixed the problem in about 1 hour, happily washed my van for me at no additional charge, and they said it was fine to keep the same tires.  I paid for the service, and the service consultant suggested I contact MB Santa Rosa and ask them to refund their service charge since they obviously missed the problem; a potentially life-threatening problem.

A few days later I called Matt at Santa Rosa, explained the situation, and he said he would talk to his boss and get back to me the next day.  Two days later I still hadn't heard back from Matt so I left a voicemail.  Another two days later, after no response, I left another voicemail for Matt.  I suppose he was hoping I would just give up and go away.  After 9 days and 4 calls to Matt with no response, I changed tactics and got a hold of Lisa in service who seemed genuinely interested in helping me.

Sure enough, later that day I finally got a call back from Matt and he regretted to inform me that since they actually provided me with a service (suggesting I buy new tires) the service charge would not be refunded.  I protested saying they misdiagnosed the problem; it had nothing to do with the tires, in fact they were still on the van and it was driving perfectly now!  Matt responded that doctors misdiagnose patients all the time but they still get paid, so they would NOT refund me.  I have never experienced such blatantly unethical behavior from any mechanic anywhere, and especially not from a Mercedes dealer.

So, unless you enjoy paying for faulty service that could potentially kill you, and terrible customer service that doesn't return your calls, take your business elsewhere.<//text>< pics>

<userid>102279740365330783777</userid><username>Elias Martinez</username><Time>1604086903719< /Time>< rate>
1<//rate>
< review>
During a global pandemic, we expect restaurants to uphold the highest standards for COVID-19 Compliance. This is exactly what I did not get during my last visit, and now it has me and my family scrambling for a COVID-19 test.

We ordered the Family Meal for 2. Chicken skewers were good, but the bulgur pilaf rice smelled and tasted off. We contacted PKG and a manager, Connie, requested that we return the food for a replacement. First of all, this got me thinking, in the nine to ten months that we have been in a GLOBAL PANDEMIC, this is the first time I have EVER heard a restaurant request to have the food brought back. The staff does not know where that bag has been, what particles it has on it, and if it is contaminated or not. Second of all, why does PKG desperately want customers to bring spoiled food back during a global pandemic? Is it to check to see if I ate half of the rice? Is it to check to see if I am lying about the quality of the food in an effort to get a free meal? What is Panini Kabob Grill insinuating towards customers by violating a MAJOR COVID-19 COMPLIANCE STANDARD just to check the validity of the customer's complaint?

I came back the next day and asked to speak to a manager, and Jesse (I believe) was quick to assist. Before I handed back the food, I asked if the PKG management staff has been put through COVID-19 Compliance training. He says that they have, but that does not have me convinced. He informed me that they do not reuse or do anything with the food other than throw it away. This, to me, was very strange. While I did see the majority of the staff wearing gloves, it really shocked me that a manager was going to take my potentially contaminated food with bare hands, and take that food back into the premises, putting the entirety of the PKG staff AND CUSTOMERS in jeopardy through potential transmission.

The general manager, Gloria, was quick to dismiss the situation and explain that it was simply a company policy. So, Panini Kabob Grill, is it company policy to do what no restaurant does during this terrifying time and put its staff and clients in jeopardy through relaxed COVID-19 Compliance Standards by taking food back? How do I know that the staff is actually following these "guidelines"? Why bring potentially contaminated food back onto the premises if it is going to be discarded?

I no longer feel safe supporting or recommending Panini Kabob Grill to any of my friends and family, because I worry for their safety during this COVID-19 pandemic. I hope this review will shed light on the irresponsible safety standards that Panini Kabob Grill strongly stands by, and potentially save you and your loved ones from being infected with this deadly virus.< /review>

<Text>Great food. In a loud and crowded restaurant.

They come hand in hand... you make good food, a lot of people want to eat it.

Panini Kabob Grill makes great food!

Hummus trio was very good. Although in a blind taste test I don't know if I could tell a huge difference between the three.

Shrimp salad was very tasty. Shrimp were big, cooked to perfection and flavorful. Although only 3 of them. Dressing had a great lemony zing.

Steak kabob was excellent. First, I like that it is cooked as a kabob, but the skewer is removed when plated, allowing the customer to eat without risk of food flying. Meat was cooked correctly and had good flavor. Grilled onions were also on point. The tomatoes and bell peppers were meh. But I am not a big cooked tomato fan.

Lastly, the banana bread pudding was everything I was expecting. Great blend of banana flavor with a sweet bread pudding. Really good.

Waitstaff were pleasant, not memorable, but not bad.

Venue is standard, clean and loud.</Text>< user>

<date>1368040966959<//date><review>This place caught my eye, and the service was as good as any decent service should be. The food however is another story. I ordered a tuna melt which, to my surprise, was the fishiest and most unfamiliar tuna sandwich I've ever had (not enjoyable). I got the servers attention to ask him if I could trade for something different, He had no problem allowing that so I ordered something simple, reliable. A turkey club panini, also no good. Turkey club from here is dry and the avocado was tough.

The worst thing about it was the bread. I was expecting a panini-pressed style sandwich. The bread I got on both sandwiches had blackened grill marks on both sides, of both slices of bread. It's as if they just panini pressed the dry bread to a crisp and then tossed the ingredients between.

They were friendly and the decor was nice and I felt bad because I've never returned food. My girlfriends dish was delicious (chicken kabob). I'm here on behalf of good panini's everywhere saying this place needs to be put in check.  Still tipped the nice waiter< /review>< Rating>
